| Life | Health Care | Primary health care | "1. Dynamic monitoring of patients’ health status using physical, laboratory, and diagnostic tests in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 2. Diagnosis and treatment of the most common infectious and non-infectious diseases, injuries, poisonings, and pathological and physiological (during pregnancy) conditions. <br> 3. Ongoing monitoring of patients diagnosed with chronic diseases (care for patients with chronic diseases and conditions), which includes a range of diagnostic and therapeutic interventions as prescribed by industry standards. <br> 4. Providing, within the scope of primary medical care, urgent medical care in the event of a physical or mental health disorder in patients, if such a disorder occurred during the patient’s appointment with a primary care physician and if the patient does not require emergency or specialized medical care. <br> 5. Referring patients who do not require emergency medical care, based on medical indications, to receive specialized medical care. <br> 6. Collaborating with providers of specialized medical care to ensure the timely diagnosis and treatment of diseases, injuries, poisonings, and pathological or physiological (during pregnancy) conditions, taking into account the specific characteristics of the patient’s health status. <br> 7. Conducting mandatory medical interventions for patients with existing risk factors for the development of specific diseases. <br> 8. Conducting preventive interventions, including: vaccination in accordance with the requirements of the immunization schedule; preparing and submitting reports on infectious diseases, food poisoning, acute occupational poisoning, and unusual reactions to vaccinations; conducting epidemiological investigations of isolated cases of infectious diseases. <br> 9. Providing counseling aimed at eliminating or reducing habits and behaviors that pose a health risk (smoking, alcohol consumption, use of other psychoactive substances, unhealthy diet, insufficient physical activity, etc.) and fostering healthy lifestyle habits. <br> 10. Monitoring uncomplicated pregnancies and (if necessary) referring patients to an obstetrician-gynecologist at a secondary care facility. <br> 11. Medical monitoring of healthy children. <br> 12. Provision of selected palliative care services to patients of all ages, including: regular assessment of the condition of critically ill patients and their needs; assessment of pain levels and treatment of pain; prescribing narcotic drugs and psychotropic substances in accordance with the law, including issuing prescriptions for the treatment of pain; prescribing treatment to manage concomitant symptoms (constipation, nausea, shortness of breath, etc.); counseling and educating caregivers; coordinating to ensure the patient’s medical, psychological, and other needs are met. <br> 13. Referring patients, based on medical indications, to receive palliative care beyond the scope of primary medical care. <br> 14. Prescribing medications, medical devices, and technical aids for medical rehabilitation, and preparing the relevant documentation in accordance with legal requirements. <br> 15. Maintaining primary medical records, issuing certificates, sick leave forms, and referrals for medical and social evaluations, as well as medical death certificates. <br> 16. Cooperation with social services for patients whose social living conditions affect their health, ensuring measures aimed at: <br> identifying and documenting cases of domestic violence and gender-based violence, in accordance with the Procedure for Conducting and Documenting the Results of Medical Examinations of Victims of Domestic Violence or Persons Who Have Likely Suffered from Domestic Violence, and providing them with medical care, approved by Order of the Ministry of Health of Ukraine No. 278 dated February 1, 2019, registered with the Ministry of Justice of Ukraine on March 14, 2019, under No. 262/33233; <br> informing victims of violence about their rights, available measures, and social services they can access, including the possibility of receiving free legal aid in accordance with the law. <br> 17. Collaboration with public health system entities. <br> 18. Providing psychosocial assistance and psychosocial services related to public mental health (provided that the necessary conditions are met and the provider has completed specialized training under the certified mhGAP program) in accordance with Order No. 2118 of the Ministry of Healthof Ukraine No. 2118 of December 13, 2023, “On the Organization of the Provision of Psychosocial Assistance to the Population,” registered with the Ministry of Justice of Ukraine on January 25, 2024, under No. 126/41471.” |  | Ministry of Health |
| Life | Health Care | Inpatient palliative care for adults and children | "1.    Assessing the patient’s condition in accordance with the criteria for identifying patients in need of palliative care. <br> 2.    Assessing the patient’s somatic condition and monitoring impairments in the functions of vital organs and systems, followed by a review and adjustment, if necessary, of the patient’s care plan. <br> 3.	Assess patients’ pain using specialized scales and prevent the development of chronic pain syndrome. <br> 4.    Assess, correct, and monitor nutritional status.  <br> 5.    Develop a patient care plan that addresses the patient’s physical, psychological, emotional, social, and spiritual needs and agreed-upon goals. <br> 6.    Conducting necessary laboratory tests, including: <br> a.    complete blood count; <br> b.    glucose in whole blood or serum; <br> c.    urinalysis. <br> 7.    Conducting necessary diagnostic tests, including: electrocardiography (ECG). <br> 8.    Providing specialized palliative care aimed at optimizing the patient’s condition, functioning, and quality of life for the following patient groups: <br> a.    patients over 65 years of age with significant mental or behavioral disorders caused by mental illness, age-related organic brain damage, or a physical condition; <br> b.    patients with complex needs resulting from age-related conditions. <br> 9.    Medical supervision and round-the-clock nursing care. <br> 10.    Respect for the patient’s right to be with family members, regardless of the patient’s condition, until the end of his or her life. <br> 11.    Provision of meals for the patient during hospitalization. <br> 12.    Providing the patient with assistive and technical mobility devices for the entire duration of hospitalization. <br> 13.    Referring the patient for inpatient treatment and diagnosis in departments or healthcare facilities specializing in the relevant field of medical care, including intensive care units (when medically indicated). Calling in specialists to the healthcare facility where the patient is receiving palliative care if it is not possible to transport the patient. <br> 14.    Providing palliative care using telemedicine methods and tools (teleconsultation/teleconference in real time or on a delayed basis, telediagnostics, remote monitoring, and telemetry) in conjunction with examinations and the use of other methods that do not conflict with the law. <br> 15.    Provision of medications, in particular, for symptomatic therapy, which are supplied through centralized procurement by the Ministry of Health, funded by other programs of the central and local budgets, as well as medications specified in the National List of Essential Medicines, necessary medical devices, and consumables in accordance with industry standards in the field of healthcare and medical-technological documents. <br> 16.    Training family members of the patient (legal representatives and caregivers) in the skills needed to care for a person requiring palliative care.  <br> 17.    Adherence to the principles of accessibility and inclusion when providing medical and/or rehabilitative care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with applicable laws and regulations. <br>  <br> Additional requirements regarding the scope of medical services that the provider undertakes to provide under the contract in accordance with the patient’s medical needs (specification) <br>  <br> 1.    Conducting an assessment of the patient’s condition at all stages (stable, unstable, deteriorating, terminal) of palliative care to determine his or her physical, cognitive, psychosocial, and other limitations. <br> 2.    Conducting the necessary laboratory tests, including: <br> a.    biochemical blood analysis (total protein, alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, urea, uric acid; electrolytes: potassium, chloride, sodium, magnesium), C-reactive protein;  <br> b.    bacteriological tests; <br> c.    other laboratory tests in accordance with industry standards. <br> 3.    Conducting necessary diagnostic imaging studies, including: <br> a.         ultrasound examinations; <br> b.    X-ray examinations; <br> c.    other diagnostic imaging studies in accordance with industry standards. <br> 4.    Provision of specialized palliative care by a multidisciplinary team to the patient with the aim of optimizing his or her health, functioning, and quality of life. <br> 5.    Treatment of chronic pain syndrome (in particular, using narcotic drugs, psychotropic substances, and precursors). <br> 6.    Timely pain relief at all stages of palliative care: mandatory anesthesiological support during all invasive diagnostic and other therapeutic procedures that require it, and round-the-clock access to non-narcotic and narcotic analgesics. <br> 7. | Life | Health Care | Treatment of Adults and Children Using Organ Transplantation | I. Pre-transplant period (prior to surgery). Service 1. <br> 1.        Examination, assessment, and ongoing monitoring of the condition of a patient who is a candidate for organ transplantation. <br> 2.        Examination, consultation, and assessment of the condition of a patient identified as a potential donor (in the case of living donation) for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation. <br> 3.        Conducting the necessary laboratory tests for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation, specifically: <br> a.         determination of blood type and Rh factor, including ABO blood group screening; <br> b.         general clinical tests (complete blood count; blood cell morphology; urinalysis); <br> c.         biochemical tests (total protein, alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), alkaline phosphatase (ALP), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, procalcitonin (quantitative determination), urea, uric acid, electrolytes (sodium, potassium, magnesium, calcium, chloride); glucose in whole blood or serum; glycated hemoglobin; C-peptide; C-reactive protein (CRP, quantitative determination), blood gas analysis, natriuretic peptides, gamma-glutamyl transpeptidase (GGT); <br> d.         determination of lipid profile parameters: triglycerides, total cholesterol, low-density lipoproteins (LDL), high-density lipoproteins (HDL) in serum; <br> e.         determination of coagulation and hemostasis parameters (thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR), fibrinogen, prothrombin index, D-dimer); <br> f.          conducting tests to detect: <br>                       i.          HIV infection: antibodies to HIV; <br>                     ii.          hepatitis B: HBsAg, anti-HBcor, anti-HBs, HBV DNA (by PCR); <br>                    iii.          hepatitis C: total antibodies (anti-HCV). HCV RNA (by PCR); <br>                    iv.          cytomegalovirus infection: viral DNA (by PCR), and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>                      v.          Epstein-Barr virus: viral DNA (by PCR) and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>                    vi.          syphilis; <br>                  vii.          SARS-CoV-2: RNA (by PCR) and/or SARS-CoV-2 antigen detection. <br> g.        immunogenetic screening: <br> i.        HLA genotyping for loci A, -B, -C, -DR, -DQ; <br> ii.   complement-dependent lymphocytotoxicity (CDLT) test using donor lymphocytes; <br> h.           testing for tumor markers; <br> i. hormone level testing: thyroxine (total T4, free T4), triiodothyronine (total T3, free T3), thyroid-stimulating hormone (TSH); parathyroid hormone (PTH); <br> j. bacteriological testing; <br> k.           conducting pathomorphological examinations (histological, cytological, immunohistochemical); <br> l.           other laboratory tests depending on the patient’s diagnosis and clinical condition, in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 4.        Conducting the necessary laboratory tests for a patient identified as a potential donor (in the case of living donation) for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation, specifically: <br> a.          determination of blood type and Rh factor; specifically, ABO blood group screening; <br> b.         general clinical tests (complete blood count; blood cell morphology; urinalysis); <br> c.          biochemical tests (total protein, alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, procalcitonin (quantitative determination), urea, uric acid, electrolytes (sodium, potassium, calcium); glucose in whole blood or serum; C-reactive protein (CRP, quantitative determination); <br> d.         determination of lipid profile parameters: triglycerides, total cholesterol, low-density lipoproteins (LDL), high-density lipoproteins (HDL) in serum; <br> e.          determination of antinuclear antibody (ANA) levels; <br> f.          assessment of coagulation and hemostasis parameters (thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR), fibrinogen, prothrombin index, D-dimer); <br> g.         conducting tests to detect: <br>                  i.          HIV infection: antibodies to HIV; <br>                ii.          hepatitis B: HBsAg, anti-HBcor, anti-HBs, HBV DNA (by PCR); <br>              iii.          hepatitis C: total antibodies (anti-HCV). HCV RNA (by PCR); <br>              iv.          cytomegalovirus infection: viral DNA (by PCR) and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>                v.          Epstein-Barr virus: viral DNA (by PCR) and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>              vi.          syphilis; <br>             vii.          SARS-CoV-2: RNA (by PCR) and/or SARS-CoV-2 antigen detection; <br> h.         conducting immunogenetic screening: <br> i.        HLA genotyping for loci A, B, C, DR, and DQ; <br> ii.   performing a complement-dependent lymphocytotoxicity test using the recipient’s serum; <br> i.       testing for tumor markers; <br> j.           pathomorphological studies (histological/cytological, immunohistochemical); <br> k.         other laboratory tests depending on the patient’s diagnosis and clinical condition, in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 5.        Conducting the necessary imaging studies for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation, specifically: <br> a.  radiological examinations; <br> b. computed tomography (including intravenous contrast, with volumetry as needed) and/or magnetic resonance imaging (including intravenous contrast); <br> c.          angiographic examination of blood vessels at a healthcare facility or under lease, contract, or other terms of use; <br> d.         ultrasound examinations, including Doppler imaging; <br> e.      endoscopic examinations; <br> f.      functional tests, specifically: <br>             i.         electrocardiography (ECG); <br>           ii.         spirometry; <br> g.     other diagnostic tests in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 6.        Conducting the necessary diagnostic tests for a patient identified as a potential donor (in the case of living donation) for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation, specifically: <br> a.      radiological examinations; <br> b.     computed tomography (including intravenous contrast) and/or magnetic resonance imaging (including intravenous contrast); <br> c.      ultrasound examinations, including Doppler imaging; <br> d.     endoscopic examinations; <br> e.      functional tests, including: electrocardiography (ECG); <br> f.      other diagnostic tests in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 7.        Consultations by other specialists for the patient undergoing organ transplantation and the potential donor, in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 8.        Providing anesthesiological care during diagnostic tests for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation, as well as for a potential donor. <br> 9.        Registration of a patient who is a candidate for organ transplantation and/or who has been identified as a potential donor (in the case of living donation) in the Unified State Information System for Organ and Tissue Transplantation (EDIST). <br> 10.        Providing counseling to patients who are candidates for organ transplantation, as well as to potential donors, regarding a healthy lifestyle (the need to quit smoking and avoid alcohol abuse, the importance of a healthy diet, weight loss, etc.). <br> 11.        Providing psychological support to patients who are candidates for organ transplantation, as well as to potential donors. <br> 12.        Adhering to the principles of accessibility and inclusion when providing medical care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with applicable laws and regulations <br> 13.        Issuing an electronic referral to a patient undergoing organ transplantation for inpatient treatment related to the transplantation and/or for other reasons. <br> 14.        Issuing an electronic referral to a potential donor for inpatient treatment to undergo an organ donation procedure. <br>  <br> I. Transplantation Period. Service 2.  <br> The scope of medical services that the provider undertakes to provide under the contract in accordance with the patient’s medical needs (specification) <br> 1.        Preoperative evaluation of the patient prior to organ transplantation surgery to establish a donor-recipient match in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 2.        Preoperative examination of the patient scheduled for organ transplantation or the living donor by a transplant surgeon, an anesthesiologist, and other specialists. <br> 3.        Conducting laboratory tests, including: <br> a.        complete blood count (24/7); <br> b.        determination of blood type and Rh factor, including ABO immunohaematological screening (24/7); <br> c.        Biochemical blood tests (24 hours a day): total protein, alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, procalcitonin (quantitative determination), urea, uric acid, electrolytes (sodium, potassium, magnesium, calcium, chloride); glucose in whole blood or serum; C-reactive protein (CRP, quantitative determination), blood gas analysis; <br> d.  coagulation and hemostasis (24-hour monitoring): thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR), fibrinogen, prothrombin index, D-dimer, testing of the patient’s infectious status to detect the presence or absence of: <br>                       i.          HIV infection: antibodies to HIV; <br>                     ii.          hepatitis B: HBsAg, anti-HBcor, anti-HBs. HBV DNA  (by PCR); <br>                    iii.          hepatitis C: total antibodies (Anti-HCV). HCV RNA  (by PCR); <br>                    iv.          cytomegalovirus infection: viral DNA (by PCR) and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>                      v.          Epstein-Barr virus: viral DNA (by PCR) and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>                    vi.          syphilis; <br>                  vii.          SARS-CoV-2: RNA (by PCR) and/or SARS-CoV-2 antigen detection; <br> e.        immunogenetic screening: <br> i.              HLA genotyping for loci A, B, C, DR, and DQ; <br> ii.            complement-dependent lymphocytotoxicity test using donor lymphocytes; <br> iv.            testing for de novo HLA antibodies; <br> v.            detection of HLA antibodies with complement-fixing activity; <br> f.        determination of blood concentrations of immunosuppressive drugs; <br> g.        complete urinalysis (24-hour); <br> h.        bacteriological tests; <br> i.        pathomorphological examinations (histological/cytological, immunohistochemical); <br> j.        other laboratory tests in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 4.        24-hour diagnostic imaging examinations, including: <br> a.  electrocardiography (ECG); <br> b.  ultrasound examinations, including Doppler and echocardiography; <br> c.  endoscopic examinations; <br> d.  radiographic examinations (including those with intravenous contrast); <br> e.  angiographic examination of blood vessels; <br> f.  computed tomography (including with intravenous contrast) and/or magnetic resonance imaging (including with intravenous contrast); <br> g.     other diagnostic tests in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 5.        Consultations with other specialists for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation or for a living donor, in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 6.        Transportation and delivery of anatomical material to the facility where the patient(s) will undergo transplant surgery.  <br> 7.        Performing surgical transplantation of a donor organ on the patient. <br> 8.        Performing the surgical procedure to remove the donor organ from the living donor. <br> 9.        Providing anesthesiological care and timely pain relief at all stages of the perioperative period, as well as during diagnostic and therapeutic procedures for the patient undergoing organ transplantation or for the living donor. <br> 10.        Provision of medical care in an intensive care unit for a patient who is to undergo organ transplantation or for a living donor. <br> 11.        Round-the-clock medical supervision and nursing care for a patient who is scheduled to undergo an organ transplant or for a living donor. <br> 12.        Administration of drug therapy, including immunosuppressive therapy (induction therapy), throughout the patient’s hospitalization. <br> 13.        Providing blood components and blood products on a 24-hour basis. <br> 14.        Administering parenteral nutrition (total or partial) to the patient. <br> 15.        Treating complications, particularly those related to early graft rejection. <br> 16.        Providing the patient with rehabilitation services during the acute phase (in the absence of contraindications) in an inpatient setting and referring the patient for rehabilitation care during the post-acute and long-term phases of rehabilitation. <br> 17.        Providing psychological support to patients undergoing organ transplantation, as well as to living donors. <br> 18.        Referring the patient to other healthcare facilities for specialized medical care in other fields, or summoning specialists from those facilities to provide such care to the patient if transportation is not possible. <br> 19.        Provision of medications procured through centralized purchasing by the Ministry of Health, funded through other programs of the central and local budgets, as well as medications specified in the National List of Essential Medicines, necessary medical devices, and consumables in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector and medical-technological documents. <br> 20.        Providing meals during inpatient care. <br> 21.        Adherence to the principles of accessibility and inclusion in the provision of medical care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with regulatory and legal acts <br>  <br> III. Post-transplant patient care. Service 3. <br> The scope of medical services that the provider undertakes to provide under the contract in accordance with the patient’s medical needs (specification) <br>  <br> 1.        Ongoing monitoring of the patient’s health status during the post-transplant period in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 2.        Conducting the necessary laboratory tests for the patient, including: <br> a.          general clinical tests (complete blood count; blood cell morphology; urinalysis); <br> b.        biochemical tests (total protein, alpha-amylase, lipase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, procalcitonin (quantitative determination), urea, uric acid, electrolytes (sodium, potassium, magnesium, calcium, phosphorus, chloride); glucose in whole blood or serum; glycated hemoglobin; C-peptide; C-reactive protein (CRP, quantitative determination); N-terminal pro-brain natriuretic peptide (NT-proBNP); glomerular filtration rate (eGFR); <br> c.          determination of lipid profile parameters: triglycerides, total cholesterol, low-density lipoproteins (LDL), high-density lipoproteins (HDL) in serum; <br> d.         determination of coagulation and hemostasis parameters (thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR), fibrinogen, D-dimer); <br> e.        fecal occult blood test; <br> f.        detection of antinuclear antibodies (ANA); <br> g.        infectious disease screening: <br>                   i.          HIV infection:  antibodies to HIV; <br>                 ii.          hepatitis B: HBsAg, anti-HBcor, anti-HBs. HBV DNA (by PCR); <br>                iii.          Hepatitis C: total antibodies (Anti-HCV). HCV RNA (by PCR); <br>                iv.          Cytomegalovirus infection: viral DNA (by PCR), and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>                  v.          Epstein-Barr virus: viral DNA (by PCR) and immunoglobulins M and G; <br>                vi.          syphilis; <br>          vii.          SARS-CoV-2: RNA (by PCR) and/or detection of SARS-CoV-2 antigen. <br> h.         immunogenetic screening: <br> i.  testing for de novo-formed antibodies to HLA; <br> ii. detection of antibodies to HLA with complement-fixing activity. <br> i.           testing for tumor markers; <br> j.       determination of blood concentrations of immunosuppressive drugs, including tacrolimus, cyclosporine, sirolimus, etc.; <br> k.         determination of hormone levels; <br> l.           conducting bacteriological tests; <br> m.   conducting pathomorphological studies (histological/cytological, immunohistochemical); <br> n.   conducting other laboratory tests as needed by the patient in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 3.        Conducting necessary diagnostic imaging studies for the patient, including: <br> a.          X-ray examinations; <br> b.         computed tomography (including intravenous contrast) and/or magnetic resonance imaging (including intravenous contrast); <br> c.          angiographic examination of blood vessels; <br> d.         ultrasound examinations, including Doppler ultrasound; <br> e.          endoscopic examinations; <br> f.          functional tests: <br>             i.         electrocardiography (ECG); <br>               ii.         spirometry. <br> g.         other diagnostic tests in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 4.        Anesthesiological support during diagnostic tests performed on the patient. <br> 5.        Prescription and/or adjustment of medication, including therapeutic drug monitoring and adjustment of immunosuppressive therapy (maintenance therapy). <br> 6.        Issuance of electronic prescriptions for immunosuppressive medications covered by the reimbursement program in accordance with applicable law. <br> 7.        Ensuring the patient’s adherence to treatment and preventing long-term consequences of immunosuppression—malignant tumors, infections, and premature cardiovascular diseases—in particular through appropriate screening. <br> 8.        Conducting dynamic monitoring of the course of pregnancy in women during the post-transplant period in collaboration with an obstetrician-gynecologist, including monitoring the health status of pregnant women, ensuring the completeness of examinations and consultations, and implementing therapeutic and preventive measures in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 9.        Providing psychological support to the patient. <br> 10.        Assessing the patient’s nutritional status and correcting it in case of deficiencies. <br> 11.        Providing counseling to the patient on healthy lifestyle choices (the need to quit smoking and avoid alcohol abuse, the importance of a healthy diet, weight loss, etc.), vaccinations, contraception for women during the first year after transplantation, mental health support, etc. <br> 12.        Educating the patient on keeping a log of vital signs (temperature, pulse, blood pressure) and recognizing early symptoms of rejection. <br> 13.        Referring the patient when indicated for specialized medical care and rehabilitation services. <br> 14.        Informing the patient about the possibility of receiving other necessary medical services free of charge through the Medical Guarantees Program. <br> 15.        Adhering to the principles of accessibility and inclusion when providing medical care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with applicable laws and regulations. |  | Ministry of Health |
| Life | Health Care | Treatment of Adults and Children Using Hematopoietic Stem Cell Transplantation | 1. Close monitoring of the recipient’s condition throughout treatment with hematopoietic stem cell transplantation (HSCT). <br> 2.     Conducting the necessary laboratory tests for the hematopoietic stem cell (HSC) recipient, specifically: <br> a.        a comprehensive clinical blood count using an automated hematology analyzer; cytomorphological examination of blood cells, differential white blood cell count (white blood cell differential); reticulocyte count (24-hour monitoring), and blood immunophenotyping according to the C, D, E, and Kell systems; <br> b.       blood type and Rh factor determination (available 24 hours a day); <br> c.        Biochemical blood analysis (electrolytes: chloride, potassium, sodium, calcium, phosphorus), glucose, total protein, C-reactive protein (quantitative determination), alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, urea, uric acid, blood pH (24-hour monitoring); gamma-glutamyl transpeptidase (GGT), lactate dehydrogenase (LDH), alkaline phosphatase (ALP), ferritin, serum iron level, β2-microglobulin; transferrin, serum iron-binding capacity, folic acid, vitamin B12, haptoglobin, procalcitonin; albumin; <br> d.       determination of lipid profile parameters: triglycerides, total cholesterol, low-density lipoproteins (LDL), high-density lipoproteins (HDL) in serum; <br> e.        coagulation and hemostasis (fibrinogen, thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR), D-dimer (24-hour monitoring), antithrombin III, thromboelastometry; <br> f.        determination of protein fractions by electrophoresis (M-protein level) and immunofixation of serum and urine proteins (detection of heavy chains of immunoglobulins IgG, IgA, IgM, and light free kappa and lambda chains); <br> g.       determination of the levels and types of normal immunoglobulins IgG, IgA, IgM, and IgE in serum; <br> h.       cytomorphological examination of cerebrospinal fluid using the liquid cytology method, biochemical analysis of cerebrospinal fluid; <br> i.         urine analysis: general, according to Nechiporenko, according to Zimnitsky, for 24-hour microalbuminuria and creatinineuria; <br> j.         determination of protein levels in 24-hour urine and Bence-Jones protein; <br> k.       flow cytometry of bone marrow aspirates and/or peripheral blood cells, counting of lymphocyte subpopulations by flow cytometry (immunogram); <br> l.         cytochemical and cytomorphological examination of bone marrow aspirate with differential count (myelogram); <br> m.     molecular genetic analysis of bone marrow cells, peripheral blood cells, and other biological material; cytogenetic analysis (using FISH and karyotyping); <br> n.       pathomorphological studies (histological and immunohistochemical examination of tumor biopsies and bone marrow trephine biopsies); <br> o.       cytological studies, including cytocentrifugates of biological fluids; <br> p.   Conducting immunogenetic screening—for healthcare facilities performing allogeneic HSCT: <br>                   i. HIV infection: antigen, specifically p24 antigen and total antibodies to HIV types 1 and 2, HIV RNA (by PCR, quantitative method) <br>                  ii.          hepatitis B: HBsAg, anti-HBcor, anti-HBs. HCV RNA (PCR, quantitative method), IgM, and IgG; <br>                iv.          hepatitis E: immunoglobulin G; <br>                  v.          cytomegalovirus infection: viral DNA (PCR, quantitative method), IgM, and IgG; <br>                vi. SARS-CoV-2: RNA (PCR, quantitative method); <br>                xi.          herpes simplex virus (HSV) types 1 and 2, type 3 (Varicella Zoster), and herpesvirus 6 (HHV-6): DNA (by PCR, quantitative method), IgM, and IgG; <br>              xii. Examination, counseling, and assessment of the condition of the HSC donor (for healthcare facilities performing allogeneic HSCT). <br> 5. Conducting conditioning procedures for the recipient patient: myeloablative and/or immunosuppressive chemotherapy and/or radiation therapy. <br> 11.        Providing oxygen support to the donor or recipient. <br> 12.        Conducting round-the-clock monitoring of vital signs (heart rate, blood pressure, SpO₂, ECG monitoring, etc.) for the recipient. <br> 13.        Providing round-the-clock medical supervision and nursing care for the recipient patient. <br> 14.        Performing a GSK transfusion (reinfusion—autologous GSK) on the recipient patient (transplantation). <br> 15.        Timely pain management at all stages of diagnosis and treatment: anesthesiological support during all invasive diagnostic procedures, round-the-clock access to non-narcotic and narcotic analgesics. <br> 16.        Close monitoring of the condition of the transplant recipient during the post-transplant period. <br> 17.        Prescription and/or adjustment of medication, including therapeutic drug monitoring and adjustment of immunosuppressive therapy for HSC recipients. <br> 18.        Treatment of complications, particularly those associated with early graft rejection (acute and chronic graft-versus-host disease). <br> 19.        Assessment of the patient’s psychological and emotional state and provision of psychological support at all stages of care. <br> 20.        Consultations for the patient by physicians of other specialties. <br> 21.        Referring the patient to other departments or healthcare facilities for specialized medical care in other fields, particularly for radiation therapy, or summoning specialists from these facilities to provide such care to the patient if transportation is not possible. <br> 22.        Providing healthcare rehabilitation services based on medical indications during treatment and referring the patient to receive rehabilitation services or palliative care services. <br> 23.        Informing the patient about possible reproductive dysfunction before starting treatment and referring him or her (if desired) for a consultation with a reproductive specialist at the appropriate healthcare facility.  <br> 24.        Providing blood components and blood products on a 24-hour basis.  <br> 25.        Providing medications, including solutions for parenteral nutrition, which are supplied through centralized procurement by the Ministry of Health, funded through other programs of the central and local budgets, as well as medications specified in the National List of Essential Medicines, necessary medical devices, and consumables in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector and medical-technological documents. <br> 26.        Providing necessary therapeutic nutrition in an inpatient setting. <br> 27.        Adherence to the principles of accessibility and inclusion in the provision of medical care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with regulatory and legal acts. |  | Ministry of Health |
| Life | Health Care | Inpatient care for adults and children without surgical procedures | 1.        Conducting an initial examination of the patient to determine his or her referral path. <br> 2.        Conducting laboratory tests, including: <br> a.        complete blood count; <br> b.        blood type and Rh factor; <br> c.        blood chemistry panel (total protein, albumin, globulin, alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, urea, uric acid, electrolytes: potassium, chloride, sodium, magnesium, calcium; ferritin; serum procalcitonin, troponin I or T, high-sensitivity (hs-cTnI); gamma-glutamyl transpeptidase (GGT), alkaline phosphatase, antinuclear antibody (ANA) titer; glycated hemoglobin, glucose; <br> d.        lipid profile: triglycerides, total cholesterol, low-density lipoproteins (LDL), high-density lipoproteins (HDL) in serum; <br> e.        Rheumatological and acute-phase markers (rheumatoid factor [quantitative], sialic acids, C-reactive protein [quantitative], antistreptolysin O [quantitative]); <br> f.        coagulation and hemostasis (thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), fibrinogen, international normalized ratio (INR)); <br> g.        whole blood glucose;  <br> h.        oral glucose tolerance test; <br> i.        cerebrospinal fluid analysis; <br> j.        urinalysis; <br> k.        microalbumin in urine; <br> l.        ketones (acetone) in urine; <br> m.        stool analysis; <br> n.        testing for syphilis, hepatitis, HIV, SARS-CoV-2, and influenza; <br> o.        bacteriological tests to identify pathogenic flora, opportunistic and obligate bacteria, as well as micro-precipitation for syphilis, detection of protozoa and helminths in stool, serotyping, and susceptibility testing for antimicrobial therapy; <br> p.        other laboratory tests in accordance with industry standards. <br> 3.        Conducting diagnostic imaging studies, including: <br> a.        electrocardiography (ECG); <br> b.        ultrasound examinations, including Doppler imaging; <br> c.        endoscopic examinations; <br> d.        radiological examinations, including computed tomography (CT) (in particular, with intravenous contrast); <br> e.        magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) (in particular, with intravenous contrast); <br> f.        other diagnostic imaging studies in accordance with industry standards. <br> 4.        Timely pain management at all stages of diagnosis and treatment: mandatory anesthesiological support during all invasive diagnostic and other therapeutic procedures that require it, and round-the-clock access to non-narcotic and narcotic analgesics. <br> 5.        Provision of oxygen support to the patient as needed. <br> 6.        Provision of medical care aimed at alleviating, relieving, or eliminating the symptoms and manifestations of a disease or other health impairment; normalizing disrupted vital processes; and facilitating the patient’s recovery and restoration of health without the use of surgical procedures. <br> 7.        Providing intensive care to the patient in the event of life-threatening conditions. <br> 8.        Providing consultations by physicians of other specialties at healthcare facilities or under contract. <br> 9.        Providing patients with rehabilitation services during the acute phase of rehabilitation (in the absence of contraindications) in an inpatient setting and referring patients to receive rehabilitation care during the post-acute and long-term phases of rehabilitation.  <br> 10.        Providing medical care to pregnant women with complicated pregnancies and/or extragenital pathologies. <br> 11.        Ensuring round-the-clock medical supervision and nursing care. <br> 12.        Conducting disease prevention measures. <br> 13.        Referring patients (as needed) to other healthcare facilities or departments to receive specialized and palliative medical care. <br> 14.        Informing patients and/or caregivers or relatives about receiving free medical services and medications during inpatient care. <br> 15.        Providing medications procured through centralized purchasing by the Ministry of Health, funded by other programs of the central and local budgets, as well as medications specified in the National List of Essential Medicines, necessary medical devices, and consumables in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector and medical-technological documents. <br> 16.        Provision of meals in an inpatient setting. <br> 17.        Provision of medical care via telemedicine (teleconsultation/teleconference in real time or on a delayed basis, telediagnosis, remote monitoring, and telemetry). <br> 18.        Adherence to the principles of accessibility and inclusion when providing medical and/or rehabilitative care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with applicable laws and regulations. <br>   <br> Additional requirements regarding the scope of medical services that the provider undertakes to provide under the contract in accordance with the patient’s medical needs (specification) (for the provision of medical care to children): <br> 1. Round-the-clock conduct of diagnostic tests in an inpatient setting for providers offering urgent medical care. <br> 3.        Conducting laboratory tests 24 hours a day at healthcare facilities. <br>  <br>   <br> Additional requirements regarding the scope of medical services that the provider undertakes to provide under the contract in accordance with the patient’s medical needs (specification) (for the provision of medical care to adults): <br>   <br> 1.        Provision of medical care to adults with acute and chronic conditions, including in the intensive care unit, in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 2.        Round-the-clock diagnostic testing in inpatient settings at healthcare facilities for providers offering emergency medical care. <br> 3.        Conducting laboratory tests 24 hours a day at healthcare facilities. |  | Ministry of Health |
| Life | Health Care | Surgical procedures for adults and children in a one-day inpatient setting | 1. Ensuring the scheduled hospitalization of a patient provided that the patient has undergone the appropriate scope of preoperative tests prior to the planned surgical procedure, performed during the outpatient phase of medical care, in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 2.        Ensuring that the patient is examined by the attending physician prior to the provision of medical services. <br> 3.        Preoperative examination of the patient by an anesthesiologist or a pediatric anesthesiologist (when providing care to children). <br> 4.        Conducting laboratory tests in the event of complications, specifically: <br> a.        complete blood count; <br> b.        coagulation and hemostasis tests (thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR)); <br> c.        glucose in whole blood or serum; <br> d.         other tests as needed by the patient. <br> 5.        Conducting additional diagnostic tests in the event of complications in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector, including ECG, X-ray, ultrasound, etc. <br> 6.        Providing medical preparation for the patient prior to diagnostic, therapeutic-diagnostic, or surgical interventions that cannot be performed on an outpatient basis. <br> 7.        Providing anesthesiological care during diagnostic, therapeutic-diagnostic, and surgical interventions/procedures. <br> 8.        Performing diagnostic, therapeutic-diagnostic, and surgical interventions/procedures that cannot be performed on an outpatient basis and require observation for no more than 24 hours in an inpatient setting. <br> 9.        Conducting, when indicated, histological and cytological examinations of material obtained during procedures in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 10.        Ensuring medical monitoring of the patient following surgical treatment or other procedures by a specialist physician, nursing staff, and an anesthesiologist if anesthesia is administered. <br> 11.        Providing postoperative pain relief when indicated, in accordance with the type of surgical procedure. <br> 12.        Providing medications procured through centralized purchasing by the Ministry of Health, funded by other programs of the central and local budgets, as well as medications specified in the National List of Essential Medicines, necessary medical devices, and consumables in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector and medical-technological documents. <br> 13.        Providing the patient with recommendations regarding further medication and rehabilitation treatment on an outpatient basis, as well as a plan of action in the event of any complications. <br> 14.        Educating the patient and/or individuals who will care for the patient after discharge from the one-day inpatient unit on the basics of postoperative care at home. <br> 15.        Providing medical care in the event of an emergency in the patient, in accordance with established referral protocols. <br> 16.        Ensuring the patient’s hospitalization in a specialized inpatient unit if complications arise during the one-day hospital stay and there are indications for round-the-clock monitoring and treatment. <br> 17.        Adhering to the principles of accessibility and inclusion when providing medical and/or rehabilitative care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with applicable laws and regulations. |  | Ministry of Health |
| Life | Health Care | Surgical procedures for adults and children in an inpatient setting | 1.          Initial examination of the patient by a physician to determine the patient’s treatment pathway. <br> 2.          Conducting laboratory tests, including: <br> a.        complete blood count; <br> b.         blood type and Rh factor determination; <br> c.        biochemical blood analysis (total protein, alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, procalcitonin (quantitative determination), urea, uric acid, electrolytes (sodium, potassium, magnesium, calcium, chloride)); <br> d.        coagulation and hemostasis (thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR)); <br> e.        glucose in whole blood or serum; <br> f.        C-reactive protein (CRP, quantitative determination); <br> g.        cerebrospinal fluid analysis; <br> h.        testing for hepatitis and HIV in accordance with industry standards; <br> i.        urinalysis; <br> j.        bacteriological tests to determine the qualitative and quantitative composition of microorganisms and their sensitivity to antimicrobial agents; <br> k.        histological examinations; <br> l.        cytological examinations; <br> m.        pathomorphological examinations; <br> n.        other laboratory tests in accordance with industry standards. <br> 3.           Conducting diagnostic imaging studies, including: <br> a.        electrocardiography (ECG); <br> b.        ultrasound examinations, including Doppler and echocardiography; <br> c.        endoscopic examinations; <br> d.        radiological examinations;  <br> e.        other diagnostic procedures in accordance with industry standards. <br> 4.        Preoperative examination of the patient by an anesthesiologist or a pediatric anesthesiologist (when providing care to children). <br> 5.        Performing the full range of surgical procedures on the patient (including open, endovascular, transcutaneous, endoscopic, and laparoscopic procedures, etc.). <br> 6.        Timely pain management, anesthesiological support, and, if necessary, procedural sedation at all stages of diagnosis and treatment, as well as round-the-clock access to non-narcotic and narcotic analgesics. Provision of anesthesia and anesthesiological monitoring during surgical procedures and examinations.  <br> 7.        Provision of intensive care to the patient in the event of life-threatening conditions. <br> 8.        Providing postoperative monitoring and follow-up medication therapy. <br> 9.        A decision by a multidisciplinary oncology team (consisting of a radiologist or radiation oncologist, an oncologist, a surgical oncologist, a gynecologic oncologist, a urologist, or a neurosurgeon, depending on the location of the disease) (consultation) regarding elective surgery for a malignant neoplasm. If a neoplasm is detected during an emergency or elective surgical procedure, histological material must be collected and examined, and the patient with suspected cancer must be referred, along with the histological findings, to a multidisciplinary (oncology) consultation (group of specialists). <br> 10.        Providing medications procured through centralized purchasing by the Ministry of Health, funded by other programs of the central and local budgets, as well as medications specified in the National List of Essential Medicines, necessary medical devices, and consumables in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector and medical-technological documents. <br> 11.        Providing round-the-clock medical supervision and nursing care for the patient. <br> 12.        Conducting consultations with physicians of other specialties. <br> 13.        Providing patients with rehabilitation services during the acute phase of rehabilitation (in the absence of contraindications) in an inpatient setting and referring the patient to receive rehabilitation care during the post-acute phase of rehabilitation.  <br> 14.        Referring patients, when indicated, to other healthcare facilities or departments for specialized and palliative care. <br> 15.        Implementing measures to prevent the development of complications. <br> 16.        Ensuring the provision of medical care via telemedicine (teleconsultation/teleconference in real-time or delayed mode, telediagnosis, remote monitoring, and telemetry). <br> 17.        Providing meals during inpatient care.  <br> 18.        Adhering to the principles of accessibility and inclusion when providing medical and/or rehabilitative care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with applicable laws and regulations. <br>   <br> Additional requirements regarding the scope of medical services that the provider undertakes to provide under the contract in accordance with the patient’s medical needs (specification) (for the provision of medical care to adults): <br> 1.        Conducting diagnostic tests on the patient in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector, specifically: <br> a.        computed tomography (CT) (including intravenous contrast) and/or magnetic resonance imaging (MRI) (including intravenous contrast) by providers offering elective surgical care; 24/7 availability—by providers offering urgent surgical care. <br> b.        Angiography by providers offering multidisciplinary medical care, including urgent surgical care. <br> c.        CT angiography by providers offering multidisciplinary medical care, including urgent surgical care. <br>   <br> 2. Round-the-clock performance of instrumental endoscopic examinations and endoscopic procedures in an inpatient setting—by providers offering urgent surgical care. <br>   <br> 3.     Round-the-clock performance of laboratory tests at healthcare facilities. <br>   <br> Additional scope of medical services that the provider undertakes to provide under the contract in accordance with the patient’s medical needs (specification) (for the provision of medical care to children): <br> 1.        Conducting necessary diagnostic imaging examinations in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector, including computed tomography (CT) scans (specifically, with intravenous contrast) with 24/7 access. <br> 2.        Conducting endoscopic examinations 24/7 in an inpatient setting. <br> 3.        Conducting laboratory tests 24 hours a day at the healthcare facility. <br> 4.        Performing surgical procedures on newborns. <br> 5.        Providing comprehensive medical care for burns of all severity levels in children in full accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 6.        Providing comprehensive medical care for injuries of all severity levels and locations in children, in full compliance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 7.        Providing comprehensive medical care to children in cases of poisoning and intoxication of all severity levels, in full compliance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 8.        Providing comprehensive medical care to children in cases where foreign bodies are detected in the sensory organs, digestive system, respiratory system, etc., in full accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. <br> 9.        Performing surgical procedures on the eyes in accordance with industry standards in the healthcare sector. |  | Ministry of Health |
| Life | Health Care | Diagnosis and treatment of adults and children with tuberculosis in inpatient and outpatient settings | 1.    Providing consultations, outpatient, and inpatient medical care to patients with tuberculosis (TB).  <br> 2.    Conducting laboratory tests:  <br> a.    complete blood count;  <br> b.    determination of blood type and Rh factor;  <br> c.    biochemical blood analysis (total protein, albumin, alpha-amylase, aspartate aminotransferase (AST), alanine aminotransferase (ALT), alkaline phosphatase, bilirubin and its fractions (total, direct, indirect), creatinine, urea, uric acid, lactic acid/lactate, electrolytes (potassium, sodium, calcium, magnesium), C-reactive protein (CRP, quantitative determination);  <br> d.    coagulation and hemostasis (thrombin time, activated partial thromboplastin time (APTT), international normalized ratio (INR));  <br> e.    thyroid-stimulating hormone (TSH);  <br> f.    glucose in whole blood or serum;  <br> g.    cerebrospinal fluid analysis;  <br> h.    urinalysis;  <br> i.    rapid tests for pregnancy, HIV, and viral hepatitis;  <br> j.    rapid tests for SARS-CoV-2 antigen; <br> k.    microscopic examination of sputum and other biological samples for acid-fast bacteria (AFB);  <br> l.    culture testing of sputum and other biological samples for Mycobacterium tuberculosis (MTB), including identification and drug susceptibility testing (DST);  <br> m.    Bacteriological examination of biological samples to identify microorganisms and determine their antibiotic resistance;  <br> n.    cytological and histological examination of biopsy specimens from affected organs;  <br> o.    molecular genetic testing of sputum and other biological specimens for the presence of MTB and resistance to antituberculosis drugs;  <br> p.    enzyme-linked immunosorbent assays (ELISAs);  <br> q.    testing for syphilis; <br> r.    other laboratory tests in accordance with industry standards. <br> 3.    Conducting necessary imaging studies, including:  <br> a.    radiological examinations, including computed tomography (CT);  <br> b.    ultrasound examinations;  <br> c.    electrocardiography (ECG);  <br> d.    endoscopic examinations, including bronchoscopy;  <br> e.    other diagnostic procedures in accordance with industry standards.  <br> 4.    Determining a treatment plan and monitoring patients with TB, including:  <br> a.    developing an individualized treatment plan for the patient during outpatient and/or inpatient care, taking into account the patient’s comorbidities;  <br> b.    assessing and fostering the patient’s adherence to treatment, identifying factors that negatively affect adherence, and adjusting the treatment plan accordingly, in particular by involving psychologists and social workers;  <br> c.    providing counseling to the patient by psychologists, tuberculosis specialists, and physicians of other specialties, including through the use of telemedicine technologies;  <br> d.    prescribing antituberculosis therapy and adjusting treatment based on the microorganisms’ sensitivity or resistance to medications, adverse reactions, the presence of comorbidities, the patient’s individual characteristics, etc.; <br> e.    determining the indications for a patient’s hospitalization and admitting the patient to the hospital if such indications exist; <br> f.    organizing outpatient treatment for tuberculosis, in particular, with the involvement of primary care physicians. <br> 5.    Ensuring the provision of drug therapy using medications supplied through centralized procurement by the Ministry of Health, as well as medications specified in the National List of Essential Medicines.  <br> 6.    Identifying, diagnosing, and treating comorbidities with the involvement of other specialists or referring the patient to receive appropriate medical services.  <br> 7.    Monitoring the effectiveness and safety of the patient’s treatment and adverse reactions to antituberculosis drugs:  <br> a.    monitoring adherence to the patient’s treatment plan;  <br> b.    monitoring the results of laboratory and instrumental examinations, microbiological tests, and other studies;  <br> c.    Monitoring adverse reactions to anti-tuberculosis drugs and ensuring adherence to established protocols when such reactions are detected, in accordance with applicable laws.  <br> 8.    Timely pain management at all stages of diagnosis and treatment: mandatory anesthesiological support during all invasive diagnostic and other therapeutic procedures.  <br> 9.    Providing the necessary care to patients with TB through a multidisciplinary team for medical, psychological, and social support, with the aim of ensuring access to necessary services and ultimately achieving effective treatment outcomes.  <br> 10.    Referring patients for rehabilitation care during the post-acute and long-term rehabilitation periods. <br> 11.    Providing emergency medical care to patients, as well as calling an emergency medical services team when necessary and providing emergency medical care until its arrival.  <br> 12.    Providing meals during inpatient care.  <br> 13.    Ensuring the provision of medical care using telemedicine methods and tools remotely (teleconsultation/teleconference in real time or on a delayed basis, telediagnosis, remote monitoring, and telemetry), along with examinations and the use of other methods that do not conflict with the law. <br> 14.    Adherence to the principles of accessibility and inclusion when providing medical and/or rehabilitative care, including through the use of telemedicine methods and tools in accordance with regulatory and legal acts. |  | Ministry of Health |

| Life | Health Care | Free hearing aids and cochlear implants | This service covers the organization and performance of cochlear implant surgeries for individuals with disabilities and children with disabilities who have severe hearing impairments. It includes:   <br> 1. Patient selection—conducted by the Medical and Social Expert Commission (MSEC) for adults and the Medical and Consultative Commission (MCC) for children. Selection is based on medical indications, a list of diagnostic tests, and the recommendations of an audiologist.   <br> 2. Surgery—implantation of the internal component of the cochlear implant system (cochlear implant, middle ear implant, bone-conduction implant, or brainstem implant) at a specialized medical facility.   <br> 3. Speech processor activation—following surgery, the device is configured, and rehabilitation is provided, which includes auditory-verbal therapy.   <br> 4. Replacement of the external component of the implant—in the event of malfunction or loss of functionality, the technical condition is assessed and, if necessary, the component is replaced based on a decision by the Medical and Social Expert Commission (MSEC) or the Medical Examination Commission (MEC).   <br> 5. Documentation and rehabilitation support—after surgery, patients receive the relevant medical reports, instructions for use, and recommendations for further medical follow-up.   <br>  <br> This service is provided by state and municipal medical facilities in accordance with legal requirements. |  | Ministry of Health |
