| Life | Education | Development, rehabilitation, and intervention | SCOPE OF SERVICES PROVIDED BY THE CHILD DEVELOPMENT CENTER AS PART OF THE REHABILITATION PATHWAY FOR INDIVIDUALS WITH SPECIAL EDUCATIONAL NEEDS AGED 0–1 <br>  <br> 1. General description of services. <br> - The Child Development Center is a preschool educational institution that provides for the physical, intellectual, and psychological development, as well as the correction of physical and intellectual development and health improvement, of children aged 2 months to 6 (7) years who receive preschool education at home or in other preschool educational institutions.  <br> - The center’s services are provided on a short-term or periodic basis, taking into account the individual needs of children, including those with special educational needs (SEN). <br> - The center promotes early social adaptation and readiness for school; it provides comprehensive educational and psychological support to children who require correction of physical and/or mental development, long-term treatment, or rehabilitation. <br>  <br> 2. Categories of service recipients. <br> Children aged 2 months to 6 (7) years, specifically: <br> - Children with SEN (based on an assessment by the Regional Educational Center). <br> - Children living in families requiring social and educational support. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Inclusive Education | "SCOPE OF SERVICES PROVIDED BY COMBINED-TYPE NURSERY-KINDERGARTENS WITHIN THE REHABILITATION PATHWAY FOR CHILDREN WITH SPECIAL EDUCATIONAL NEEDS AGED 1–3 YEARS <br>  <br> 1. General description of services. <br> - A combined-type nursery-kindergarten is a preschool education facility for children aged 1–6 (7) years, and for children with special educational needs—up to 7 (8) years.  <br> - The facility may operate various types of groups: general development, compensatory, inclusive, family, and outdoor play groups.  <br> - The educational process is organized in accordance with the Core Component of Preschool Education, taking into account the children’s health status and their cognitive, psychological, and physical development. <br>  <br> 2. Categories of service recipients. <br> - Typically developing children. <br> - Children with special educational needs (based on a conclusion from the Regional Educational Center). <br> - Children from large, low-income families and children in foster care. <br>  <br> 3. Types of groups and characteristics of their operation. <br>  <br> 3.1. General development groups: <br> These groups are designed for children without special educational needs and aim to foster harmonious personal development through: <br> - the development of thinking, attention, memory, and sensory perception; <br> - improving speech and communication skills; <br> - developing motor skills and physical endurance; <br> - engaging in creative activities through visual arts, music, and theater; <br> - gradually developing self-care skills, appropriate behavior, and effective interaction with peers. <br>  <br> 3.2. Remedial Groups: <br> Designed for children with developmental challenges and/or special educational needs. The primary goal is to provide individualized support for development, learning, and socialization through: <br> - remedial sessions with a speech-language pathologist, special education teacher, and psychologist to develop speech, cognitive, and sensory functions; <br> - using specialized physical rehabilitation techniques to improve motor skills, coordination, and overall physical condition; <br> - fostering emotional stability, overcoming anxiety, and building self-confidence; <br> - supporting the child’s adaptation to the social environment through the development of daily living and communication skills. <br>  <br> 3.3. Inclusive Groups: <br> These groups facilitate the joint participation of typically developing children and children with special educational needs, while ensuring conditions for the realization of each child’s individual educational trajectory. The work of an inclusive group involves: <br> - creating an accessible environment (barrier-free access, adherence to the principles of universal design and reasonable accommodation, assistive devices); <br> - adapting and/or modifying educational programs, spaces, and materials to meet the needs of children with special educational needs; <br> - providing the necessary material, technical, and instructional resources; <br> - support from specialists: a teacher’s assistant, a child’s assistant (if needed), a speech-language pathologist, a special education teacher, and a psychologist; <br> - individualizing the educational process, including the development and implementation of an individual development program (and, if necessary, an individualized education plan) based on the assessment report from the Regional Educational Center, with the program reviewed at least three times a year by the psychological and pedagogical support team; <br> - providing remedial, developmental, and psychological-pedagogical services in group or individual settings; <br> - supporting the child’s emotional well-being and social adaptation, and fostering a supportive atmosphere within the group; <br> - if necessary, providing social and educational support to families of children with special educational needs who do not attend the facility. <br>  <br> 3.4. Family Groups: <br> Groups with a small number of children, where an individualized approach to the child’s development is provided in an environment similar to that of home. Key features: <br> - personalized planning of the educational process, taking into account the needs and abilities of each child; <br> - upbringing in a family-like atmosphere with an emphasis on family traditions and values; <br> - organizing learning through play to develop cognitive, creative, and social skills; <br> - regular counseling support for parents regarding their child’s development, upbringing, and interaction with the child. <br>  <br> 3.5. Outdoor groups: <br> Short-term groups focused on active leisure, social interaction, and exploring the environment. Main areas of focus: <br> - organizing walks and active games to promote physical activity; <br> - forming basic concepts about nature and seasonal changes; <br> - developing communication skills through shared play activities. <br>  <br> 4. Educational Services. <br> The educational process encompasses the development, upbringing, and instruction of children in accordance with the approved educational program, which is based on the Core Component of Preschool Education. <br> Key approaches: <br> - developing key competencies through play, exploration, and creative activities; <br> - individualizing instruction to account for the child’s age, intellectual, and physical characteristics; <br> - implementing the educational process in one or more priority areas (arts and aesthetics, physical education and health, music, humanities, etc.) to support each child’s interests and develop their abilities. <br>  <br> 5. Medical care. <br> - Sanitary control at the facility and ongoing monitoring of children’s health. <br> - Monitoring compliance with individual immunization schedules and preventive health checkups. <br> - Providing first aid when necessary, informing parents about the child’s condition, and arranging hospitalization when medically indicated. <br>  <br> 6. Collaboration with Parents (Legal Guardians). <br> Systematic collaboration with parents (legal guardians) is organized to ensure the child’s sustainable development. Key areas of focus include: <br> - Regular updates on the child’s individual progress and needs; <br> - Counseling on issues related to upbringing, development, and education, particularly for children with special educational needs; <br> - conducting training sessions, parent meetings, and thematic gatherings; <br> - involving parents in joint educational, upbringing, and remedial activities; <br> - providing information on the specifics of the child’s development and how to support it within an inclusive educational environment. <br>  <br> This approach ensures that children’s individual needs are met and promotes their comprehensive development during the preschool years. <br>  <br>  <br> " |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Inclusive Education | SCOPE OF SERVICES PROVIDED BY A COMPENSATORY-TYPE DAYCARE CENTER AS PART OF THE REHABILITATION PATHWAY FOR CHILDREN WITH SPECIAL EDUCATIONAL NEEDS AGED 2–3 YEARS <br>  <br> 1. General description of services. <br> - A compensatory-type nursery-kindergarten is a preschool education institution for children with special educational needs (SEN) aged 2–7 (8) years. <br> - The institution provides care, development, health promotion, upbringing, and education for these children, taking into account their special educational needs and in accordance with the requirements of the Basic Component of Preschool Education.  <br> - These institutions are divided into special and sanatorium-type facilities. <br>  <br> 2. Categories of service recipients. <br> - Children with SEN (based on a conclusion from the Regional Educational Center). <br> - Children with disabilities (upon presentation of a medical certificate and/or an individual rehabilitation program). <br> - Children with chronic illnesses requiring long-term treatment or rehabilitation. <br>  <br> 3. Specialized nursery-kindergartens. <br> Designed for children with hearing, vision, speech, musculoskeletal, and intellectual development impairments, as well as those with delayed mental development. The main goal is to provide comprehensive corrective, developmental, and educational support tailored to the child’s individual needs. <br> Main services: <br> - Corrective and developmental sessions with a speech-language pathologist, special education teacher, and other specialists to develop speech, thinking, sensory integration, communication, and cognitive skills. <br> - Stimulation of auditory, visual, and tactile perception; development of spatial orientation. <br> - Development of independence skills, social interaction, emotional resilience, and positive self-esteem; support for adaptation to the educational environment. <br> - Development and implementation of an Individualized Education Program (IEP) by a team of psychological and pedagogical support specialists based on the findings of the Regional Educational Center (REC); the IEP is reviewed at least three times a year. <br> - Counseling parents on the child’s developmental characteristics and organizing remedial support at home. <br>  <br> 4. Sanatorium-based nurseries and kindergartens. <br> Sanatorium-based nurseries and kindergartens are designed for children with chronic diseases of the respiratory, digestive, nervous, and cardiovascular systems, as well as those with early manifestations of tuberculosis and other conditions requiring long-term treatment and rehabilitation. <br> Main services: <br> - Therapeutic exercise, massage, physical therapy procedures, and a medically prescribed diet. <br> - Daily monitoring of health status, adherence to doctors’ orders, and prevention of exacerbations. <br> - Restoration of physical functions, support of the immune system, and adaptation following illness. <br> - Implementation of educational and developmental programs that assess children’s physical condition, use individualized approaches, and incorporate play-based methods. <br> - Development of life skills, daily living independence, and communication and social skills. <br>  <br> 5. Providing a learning environment that accommodates the child’s special needs. <br> - The educational process:  <br> 1) encompasses the development, upbringing, and education of children; <br> 2) is carried out using specialized or adapted programs and methodologies that meet the child’s educational needs and are developed based on the Core Component of Preschool Education; <br> 3) is organized with consideration for the individual developmental characteristics of each child. <br> - Priority areas (art and aesthetics, physical education and health, music, humanities, etc.) are implemented with consideration for the children’s interests and needs. <br> - The educational environment is arranged in accordance with accessibility requirements, adhering to the principles of universal design and reasonable accommodation. <br> - For children not enrolled in preschool education, social and educational support for families and counseling services may be provided. <br>  <br> 6. Medical Care. <br> - Sanitary control at the facility and ongoing monitoring of children’s health. <br> - Monitoring compliance with individual immunization schedules and preventive health checkups. <br> - Providing first aid when necessary, informing parents about the child’s condition, and arranging hospitalization when medically indicated. <br>  <br> 7. Specifics of Service Delivery. <br> - Remedial and therapeutic work in specially equipped rooms. <br> - An individualized approach to each child, taking into account their physical, psychological, and educational needs. <br> - Teamwork among educators, medical staff, and psychologists to ensure the child’s comprehensive development. <br> - Ongoing collaboration with parents to support the child’s development and enhance the effectiveness of support services. <br>  <br> Compensatory-type daycare centers create favorable conditions for the development, education, and rehabilitation of children with special educational needs, helping them to realize their full potential and adapt to social life. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Inclusive Education | SCOPE OF SERVICES PROVIDED BY FAMILY-TYPE NURSERY-KINDERGARTENS AS PART OF THE REHABILITATION PATHWAY FOR CHILDREN WITH SPECIAL EDUCATIONAL NEEDS AGED 1–3 YEARS <br>  <br> 1. General description of services. <br> - A family-style nursery-kindergarten is a preschool education facility for children aged 2 months to 6 (7) years (up to 7 (8) years for children with special educational needs) who are in family relationships. <br> - Care, development, upbringing, and education of children are provided in accordance with the Basic Component of Preschool Education. <br> - The educational process is implemented in a manner similar to home-based care, taking into account each child’s individual rhythm and needs, including the needs of children with special educational needs. <br> - Groups are formed based on family ties (regardless of the degree of kinship), with the option of round-the-clock, daytime, or short-term care. <br>  <br> 2. Main Services. <br> 2.1. Care and Medical Services: <br> - Organization of a daily routine that takes into account the child’s age and physiological characteristics: alternating activities, walks, sleep, and meals according to individual needs. <br> - Meals provided in accordance with age-appropriate standards and schedules; dietary therapy as needed, in accordance with medical recommendations. <br> - Development of basic self-care skills: encouraging the child to participate in dressing, washing, and eating; gradual development of hygiene and daily living skills. <br> - Hygiene care: assistance with washing, potty training, and skin care; ensuring a safe and comfortable environment. <br> - Medical supervision: daily monitoring of the child’s condition; tracking the vaccination schedule and preventive checkups; providing first aid as needed. <br> - Sanitary and epidemiological control within the group, preventive measures, informing parents about the child’s health status, and arranging hospitalization if necessary. <br>  <br> 2.2. Educational Development: <br> - The educational process is implemented through play, communication, and everyday situations in accordance with the educational program developed on the basis of the Basic Component of Preschool Education. <br> - The main focus is on the development of speech, cognitive activity, sensory skills, and fine and gross motor skills. <br> - Children are engaged in simple exploratory activities, object-play, role-play, art, and music activities. <br> - Skills in emotional regulation, interaction with adults and peers, and the basic elements of self-esteem and independence are developed. <br> - The educational process is aimed at ensuring psychological comfort, fostering interest in interaction, and facilitating gradual adaptation to the group. <br>  <br> 2.3. Upbringing: <br> - Creating conditions for the development of early independence and teaching basic self-care skills (washing, dressing, using a spoon). <br> - Fostering socially acceptable behavior through play, daily interaction, and positive reinforcement. <br> - Developing communication skills, the ability to share, wait one’s turn, and express requests and emotions in an appropriate manner. <br> - Cultivating emotional sensitivity, empathy, and initial understanding of rules and boundaries. <br> - Fostering respect for adults and interaction with other children through accessible activities—such as group games and role-playing scenarios. <br> - Introducing family traditions and fostering a sense of belonging to the cultural environment in an age-appropriate manner (holidays, songs, simple rituals). <br>  <br> 2.4. Physical Development: <br> - Promoting the development of basic motor skills (walking, running, climbing, throwing) through specially organized active games and exercises. <br> - Ensuring daily active physical activity, outdoor walks, and age-appropriate hardening exercises. <br> - Conducting physical education classes aimed at developing coordination, balance, and endurance. <br> - For children with special educational needs—individual implementation of therapeutic physical education, massages, and physiotherapy procedures in accordance with medical indications. <br> - Developing spatial orientation skills and safe behavior while moving. <br>  <br> 3. Inclusive Education. <br> - The educational process for children with special educational needs is organized upon request by a parent (legal guardian) and based on the conclusion of the Regional Educational Center (REC) regarding a comprehensive psychological and pedagogical assessment of the child’s development. <br> - Creating an inclusive educational environment in accordance with the principles of universal design and reasonable accommodation. <br> - Development and implementation of an Individual Development Program (IDP) and, if necessary, an individualized education plan; regular monitoring of the IDP’s implementation by a team of psychological and pedagogical support specialists. <br> - Involvement of specialists (speech-language pathologist, special education teacher, psychologist, rehabilitation specialist), a teacher’s assistant, and, if necessary, a child’s personal assistant; <br> - Ensuring the adaptation and/or modification of educational programs, the learning environment, and materials, taking into account the level of support required; <br> - If necessary, providing social and educational support to families whose children are not enrolled in preschool education (to offer counseling assistance to the family). <br>  <br> 4. Collaboration with the family. <br> - Creating conditions for a partnership between the institution and the family, taking into account the age-specific needs of young children. <br> - Providing individual counseling to parents (legal guardians) regarding the child’s care, upbringing, speech development, and daily living and social skills. <br> - Involving parents in the implementation of the child’s individualized development program for children with special educational needs (if applicable), including recommendations for home activities. <br> - Conducting joint play and educational activities to build trust and a stable emotional bond between the child and adults. <br> - Continuously sharing observations regarding changes in the child’s development and using various forms of feedback with parents. <br>  <br> This approach ensures the child’s comprehensive development in an environment as close as possible to a family setting, guaranteeing the realization of their right to a quality preschool education, particularly in an inclusive educational setting. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Obtaining General Secondary Education | General secondary education institutions (GSEIs) are legal entities whose primary activity is educational work in accordance with state educational standards. They provide a comprehensive approach to the education, development, and socialization of children aged 6–18, including those with special educational needs (SEN). <br> - Educational, remedial-developmental, and counseling services are aimed at creating an inclusive educational environment and ensuring equal access to quality education. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Acquisition of General Secondary Education | Specialized educational institutions provide a complete general secondary education along with specialized training in accordance with the institution’s area of focus. <br> - Services are designed to develop the natural abilities and talents of students, including those with SEN, ensuring a comprehensive approach to education, development, and socialization. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Inclusive Education, Institutional Care | A special school is a general secondary education institution for individuals with special educational needs (SEN) resulting from intellectual disabilities, physical disabilities, and/or sensory impairments. <br> - The institution ensures the creation of a supportive educational environment and organizes instruction and development in accordance with national educational standards and the individual needs of students. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Inclusive education, institutional care | - An Educational and Rehabilitation Center (ERC) is a general secondary education institution for individuals with special educational needs (SEN), particularly those caused by complex developmental disabilities. <br> - The center provides educational services, as well as psychological, pedagogical, medical, and social rehabilitation for individuals with SEN, creating conditions for them to obtain general secondary education, develop life skills, achieve social adaptation, and prepare for independent living. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Club Activities and Extracurricular Education | An extracurricular education institution is a component of the extracurricular education system that imparts knowledge, develops skills and abilities based on interests, meets individuals’ needs for creative self-realization and intellectual, spiritual, and physical development, prepares them for active professional and civic engagement, and creates conditions for social protection and the organization of meaningful leisure activities. <br> - The institution provides services outside of school hours, taking into account the age, health status, and abilities and talents of pupils, students, and participants, including those with special educational needs. <br> - The institution conducts educational and upbringing, informational and methodological, organizational and mass outreach, training, and international activities. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Vocational and Technical Education | Vocational (vocational-technical) education institutions (VTEIs) ensure that the needs of children under 18 years of age, including those with special educational needs (SEN),  in vocational (vocational-technical) education, mastering blue-collar professions, specializations, and qualifications in accordance with their interests, abilities, and health status. <br> - As part of a child’s rehabilitation pathway, VTE institutions provide educational, practical, social, and remedial-developmental services, adapting instruction to the needs of individuals with SEN, particularly those with disabilities. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Obtaining Pre-Higher Vocational Education | - Pre-higher vocational education institutions (PHVEIs) are educational institutions that provide educational services related to the acquisition of pre-higher vocational education corresponding to the educational and professional level of an associate’s degree. Such institutions may also conduct research, creative arts, and sports activities, ensuring a combination of theoretical instruction and practical training.  <br> - They provide: theoretical and practical training for students; support for the professional development of individuals with special educational needs (SEN); inclusive education and adaptation of the educational environment to ensure equal access to education. |  | Ministry of Education and Science |
| Life | Education | Social rehabilitation, vocational and technical education | - The vocational school for social rehabilitation is a state institution of vocational (vocational-technical) education for children who require special educational conditions, falling under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Education and Science. <br> - The institution provides vocational (technical and vocational) education, general secondary education, psychological and pedagogical support, medical care, and social rehabilitation within a structured educational environment. <br> - The school’s educational regime includes a special daily schedule, constant supervision and monitoring, as well as restrictions on leaving the school grounds unaccompanied. <br> - Students (pupils) remain at the school for the period established by the court, but no longer than three years, |  | Ministry of Education and Science |

## Аркуш: «Role» (10×6)

| Код | Роль | Рівень доступу | Що бачить (Головний дашборд) | Обмеження доступу до даних | Категорія |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Ф-Г | Фахівець ССД (Громада) | Громада | Свої кейси, заявки, діти, строки, контрольні візити | Персональні дані у межах своєї громади та портфеля | Фахівець ССД |
| Ф-М | Фахівець / Нач. ССД (Місто) | Місто | Уся операційна картина по місту: заявки, діти, сімейні форми, заклади | Персональні дані по всій міській території + управлінські зведення | Фахівець з повноваженням міста |
| Ф-О | Нач. ССД / Аналітик (Область) | Область | Зведена область: громади, райони, заклади, повнота даних, аналітика | Повний територіальний доступ у межах області | Фахівець з повноваженням області |
| Н-Р | НСССУ / Регіональний контролер | Регіон | Моніторинг якості даних, контроль користувачів, інтернатний блок, ризики | Зведення + персоніфікований доступ за повноваженням | Нацсоцслужба |
| Н-Н | Мінсоцполітики / Глобал-Адмін | Національний | Національний дашборд: макро-KPI, порівняння територій, генерація звітів | Зведена аналітика по країні; персональні дані — лише за службовою потребою | Глобал Адміністратор |
| Б | Батьки (мобільний додаток ЦШД) | Власна дитина | Персональний дашборд моєї дитини: статуси, нагадування, виплати, поради | Тільки своя дитина (через Дія.Підпис) | Кінцевий користувач |
| М-В | Міжвідомчий користувач | Свій вертикальний зріз | МОЗ / МОН / МВС / Мінʼюст / ПФУ / Мінветеранів — доступ у межах компетенції | Відповідно до міжвідомчих угод і Трембіта | Міжвідомча роль |
| Адм | Адміністратор системи | Технічний | Управління користувачами, ролями, інтеграціями, моніторинг безпеки | Адмін-панель + аудит | Адміністратор |
| П | Публічний / неавторизований | Публічна частина | Тільки агреговані знеособлені показники для відкритого порталу | Публічний портал | Громадянин |
